# Refactoring Review: PR #217 -- Add `-y` flag to hooks installer invocation in `update-aimaestro.sh`

Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent
Issue: #212

## Verdict: APPROVED WITH CAVEAT

## Summary

**Refactoring Goal:** Add `-y` flag to `./scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh` call inside `update-aimaestro.sh` so the update runs non-interactively, matching all other installer invocations.

**Goal Achieved:** Partially

**Behavior Preserved:** Yes (no functional change -- see caveat)

## Diff Analysis

**File changed:** `update-aimaestro.sh` (line 262)

**Before:**
```bash
./scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh
```

**After:**
```bash
./scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh -y
```

**Change location confirmed:** Line 262 of `update-aimaestro.sh`, inside the "Step 6: Claude Code hooks" block (lines 259-264). VERIFIED by reading the actual file at `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/update-aimaestro.sh` lines 259-264.

**No other changes in the diff:** Confirmed. The diff contains only the single-line change.

## Consistency Analysis

All other installer invocations in `update-aimaestro.sh` already pass `-y` unconditionally:

| Line | Installer | Has `-y`? |
|------|-----------|-----------|
| 225 | `./install-messaging.sh -y` | Yes |
| 234 | `./install-memory-tools.sh -y` | Yes |
| 241 | `./install-graph-tools.sh -y` | Yes |
| 248 | `./install-doc-tools.sh -y` | Yes |
| 255 | `./install-agent-cli.sh -y` | Yes |
| 262 | `./scripts/claude-hooks/install-hooks.sh` | **No (this PR fixes it)** |

After this PR, all 6 installer invocations will consistently pass `-y`.

# Audit Report: PR #216 - fix(install): quote variables to prevent word-splitting

**Generated:** 2026-02-15
**Reviewer:** judge-agent
**Issue:** #211
**PR:** #216

## Verdict: APPROVED

## Summary

**Goal:** Quote two unquoted variable expansions in `install.sh` to prevent word-splitting and globbing (ShellCheck SC2086).
**Goal Achieved:** Yes
**Behavior Preserved:** Yes -- quoting these variables makes them safer without changing semantics.

## Diff Analysis

The PR contains exactly 2 changes in `install.sh`, both correct:

### Change 1: Line 293 (diff hunk @@ -281,7 +281,7 @@)

**Before:**
```bash
NODE_MAJOR=$(echo $NODE_VERSION | cut -d'.' -f1 | sed 's/v//')
```
**After:**
```bash
NODE_MAJOR=$(echo "$NODE_VERSION" | cut -d'.' -f1 | sed 's/v//')
```

**Analysis:** CORRECT. `$NODE_VERSION` contains output of `node --version` (e.g., `v20.11.0`). While this value will never contain spaces or glob characters in practice, quoting it is the correct defensive practice. The quoting does not change behavior for any valid node version string. Without quotes, if `NODE_VERSION` were empty, `echo` would output a blank line and `cut` would still work, so behavior is identical either way.

### Change 2: Line 997 (diff hunk @@ -979,7 +979,7 @@)

**Before:**
```bash
echo "   cd $INSTALL_DIR"
```
**After:**
```bash
echo "   cd \"$INSTALL_DIR\""
```

**Analysis:** CORRECT and IMPORTANT. This is inside a double-quoted `echo` so the `$INSTALL_DIR` was already protected from word-splitting by the outer quotes. However, the fix adds escaped inner quotes around the path in the _output_, which means users who copy-paste the displayed command will get `cd "/path/to/ai-maestro"` instead of `cd /path/to/ai-maestro`. This is a UX improvement -- if a user installs to a path with spaces, the displayed command will now work correctly when copy-pasted.

### No Other Changes

Confirmed: The diff contains exactly 2 hunks, each changing exactly 1 line. No other files are modified.

## Behavior Preservation

| Aspect | Before | After | Preserved? |
|--------|--------|-------|------------|
| Node version parsing | Works for all valid version strings | Identical | Yes |
| `cd` in

# PR #213 Audit Report
Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent

## Summary
**NEEDS WORK** - The fix in `convertAMPToMessage()` is correct and well-implemented, but there is a secondary propagation gap: the AMP summary builder (lines 296-309) does not copy `fromLabel`/`toLabel` from the converted Message to the MessageSummary, so list views will still lack labels.

## Verification Checklist

### 1. Imports -- PASS
Both `getAgentByName` and `getAgentByAlias` are already imported at line 6 of `lib/messageQueue.ts` from `./agent-registry`. No new imports needed.

### 2. Function Signatures -- PASS
- `getAgentByName(name: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null` (line 228, agent-registry.ts)
- `getAgentByAlias(alias: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null` (line 267, agent-registry.ts)
- Both return `Agent | null`, and the `Agent` interface has `label?: string` (line 156, types/agent.ts)

### 3. convertAMPToMessage Fix -- PASS
The fix correctly:
- Resolves agents via `getAgentByName(fromName) || getAgentByAlias(fromName)` (tries name first, then alias)
- Falls back to raw name if agent not found: `fromAgent?.label || fromName`
- Adds `fromLabel` and `toLabel` to the returned Message object
- Placement is correct (after name extraction, before return)

### 4. Fallback Behavior -- PASS
- If agent not found in registry, `fromAgent` is null, so `fromAgent?.label` is undefined, and `fromLabel` becomes `fromName` (the raw extracted name). This is correct.
- If agent found but has no label, `agent.label` is undefined, so falls back to `fromName`. Correct.

### 5. Type Correctness -- PASS
- `Message.fromLabel?: string` (line 27) and `Message.toLabel?: string` (line 33) are properly typed
- `MessageSummary.fromLabel?: string` (line 74) and `MessageSummary.toLabel?: string` (line 79) are properly typed

### 6. No Regressions to Existing Logic -- PASS
The diff only adds new lines; no existing lines are modified or removed. The new code is inserted between the `status` assignment and the `return` statement. All existing fields in the return object are untouched.

## Issues Found

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:29:36]*

Good catch by the audit agent. The `fromLabel`/`toLabel` fields were correctly added to `convertAMPToMessage()` by PR #213's diff, but the AMP summary builder that calls that function was silently dropping them. Now both code paths propagate labels to `MessageSummary`. Committed as `47423ac` and pushed.

This also means PR #213 can be simplified — its `convertAMPToMessage()` changes are now in PR #206, so #213 only needs to ensure no duplicate when merging. I'll add a note:

# Refactoring Review: PR #214 - fix(amp): preserve signature verification data in convertAMPToMessage

Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent
Issue: #208

## Verdict: APPROVED (with one advisory note)

## Summary

**Refactoring Goal:** Populate the `amp` field on `Message` objects returned by `convertAMPToMessage()` so that cryptographic verification data (signature, sender public key, AMP address, envelope ID) is not discarded during conversion.

**Goal Achieved:** Yes

**Behavior Preserved:** Yes -- no existing fields are modified; only the previously-undefined `amp` field is now populated.

## Quality Metrics

| Metric | Before | After | Verdict |
|--------|--------|-------|---------|
| Lines of Code (convertAMPToMessage) | 43 | 53 | +10 lines, acceptable |
| Missing interface fields | `amp` always undefined | `amp` populated when data exists | Fixed |
| Data loss | Signature/key discarded | Signature/key preserved | Fixed |

## Behavior Analysis

### Preserved Behaviors

- [X] `convertAMPToMessage` still returns `null` for missing envelope/payload
- [X] `convertAMPToMessage` still validates required envelope fields (id, from, to, subject)
- [X] All existing fields (id, from, fromAlias, fromHost, to, toAlias, toHost, timestamp, subject, priority, status, content, inReplyTo) are unchanged
- [X] `collectMessagesFromAMPDir` (creates `MessageSummary`, not `Message`) is unaffected
- [X] `getMessage()` callers now get richer data but no breaking changes

### Changed Behaviors

| Behavior | Before | After | Acceptable? |
|----------|--------|-------|-------------|
| `message.amp` | Always `undefined` | Object with signature data (or `undefined` if no sig/key) | Yes -- additive only |

## Data Flow Trace (VERIFIED)

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:30:16]*



Understood. I've added that as a permanent workflow rule: **double audit every PR before submission**. The process I'll follow going forward:

1. **Audit Pass 1**: Spawn judge/review agents to analyze the diff against the issue requirements, verify data flow, check for stale diffs, merge conflicts, and missing propagation
2. **Act on findings**: Fix any issues found in Pass 1
3. **Audit Pass 2**: Re-verify the fixed code — read the actual changed files, confirm the fixes are correct, check build + tests pass
4. **Only then** create or update the PR

This session demonstrated exactly why this matters — the first audit caught:
- PR #215's stale diff (POST handler redundant with PR #206)
- PR #213's missing label propagation in the summary builder
- PR #214 + #213 merge conflict risk
- 6 unquoted tmux targets across 3 files

All fixed before the PRs go to review. No more single-pass audits.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:31:20]*

Got it. **Double audit = run the full 2-pass cycle twice.** So the workflow before any PR is:

**Cycle 1:**
- Pass 1: Spawn audit agents → collect findings
- Pass 2: Fix all issues found

**Cycle 2:**
- Pass 3: Spawn audit agents again on the fixed code → verify fixes, catch anything new
- Pass 4: Fix any remaining issues

**Only then** push and create/update the PR. Four passes total, not two. I'll follow this going forward.

**Audit checklist:**
- [ ] Diff reads correctly against current file state
- [ ] Remo
... [662 more chars]

**Result:**

I've now verified everything. Let me trace the additional bug in the regex: The `-c` pattern `/\s*-c\b(?!\s*\S)/g` uses a negative lookahead `(?!\s*\S)` which means "not followed by optional whitespace then a non-whitespace character" -- effectively meaning `-c` is only matched when it's at the end of the string or followed by only whitespace. But `--continue` would already be caught by the first regex, so `-c` is the short form. The regex is actually overly conservative (it tries not to match `-c` when followed by another argument), but the fundamental issue is the `isFirstLaunch` logic being broken as the PR describes.

Now let me write the audit report.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:45:55]*

Now I have read all 5 files thoroughly. Let me do a detailed analysis and write the review.

**File 1: install-agent-cli.sh**
- VERIFIED: `set -u` removed, only `set -eo pipefail` at line 26. Correct -- `set -u` would break `${HOME:-}`, `${TERM:-}`, `${SHELL:-}` defensive defaults throughout.
- VERIFIED: Dual PATH guard at line 338: checks both `# AI Maestro` marker (any installer) AND `/.local/bin` regex pattern. The regex uses word boundary `(["'"'"':]|$)` to prevent false positives.
- VERIFIED: Daily backup limit at lines 342-349: `today_backup="${shell_config}.aimaestro-backup.$(date +%Y%m%d)"` with `if [[ ! -f "$today_backup" ]]` guard.
- All variables properly quoted throughout (`"$HOME"`, `"$INSTALL_DIR"`, etc.)
- Error handling on every critical operation (cp, chmod, mkdir, mv) with `|| { ... return 1; }`
- Atomic manifest write via temp file + mv at lines 160-185
- Signal handlers clean up staging directory

**File 2: install-doc-tools.sh**
- VERIFIED: Improved sed pattern at line 129: `sed -E 's#(source|\.) +"?\$\{?SCRIPT_DIR\}?/docs-helper\.sh"?#source "${HOME}/.local/share/aimaestro/shell-helpers/docs-helper.sh"#g'` -- handles `source` or `.`, with/without braces around SCRIPT_DIR, with/without quotes.
- VERIFIED: Substitution verification at lines 131-133: `grep -q 'SCRIPT_DIR.*/docs-helper\.sh'` post-check with WARNING on failure.
- Issue: Line 47 `shift 2` on `$@` in docs_query function -- `$@` is unquoted, will word-split if params contain spaces. But this is in a heredoc for the helper script, not installer logic.
- Minor: No `set -o pipefail` -- only `set -e`. Acceptable for this simpler script.

**File 3: install-messaging.sh**
- VERIFIED: Absolute SCRIPT_DIR at line 92: `SCRIPT_DIR="$(cd "$(dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}")" && pwd)"` -- resolves to absolute path.
- VERIFIED: Marker-based cleanup for old scripts at lines 618-630: `head -5 ... | grep -qi "AI Maestro"` before deleting -- prevents accidental deletion of user scripts with same names.
- VERIFIED: Backup before skill replace at lines 717-718: `cp -r ~/.claude/skills/agent-messaging ~/.claude/skills/agent-messaging.backup-"$(date +%Y%m%d%H%M%S)"`. Also uses temp-copy-then-swap pattern (lines 726-749) with rollback on failure.
- VERIFIED: stderr separation at lines 326-331: `print_success ... >&2` and `print_warning ... >&2`, with only `echo "$DISTRIBUTED"` on stdout for `$()` capture.
- The `distribute_shared_to_per_agent` function properly uses `while IFS= read -r` with process substitution `< <(find ...)` to avoid subshell issues.
- All `rm -rf` operations are on well-defined paths under `~/.claude/skills/`.

**File 4: install.sh**

   700→export function deleteAgent(id: string, hard: boolean = false): boolean {
   701→  const agents = loadAgents()
   702→  const agentToDelete = agents.find(a => a.id === id)
   703→
   704→  if (!agentToDelete) {
   705→    return false // Agent not found
   706→  }
   707→
   708→  const agentName = agentToDelete.name || agentToDelete.alias
   709→
   710→  // Kill all tmux sessions belonging to this agent (both soft and hard delete)
   711→  killAgentSessions(agentToDelete)
   712→
   713→  if (!hard) {
   714→    // --- Soft-delete path: mark as deleted, preserve all data on disk ---
   715→    const agentIndex = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === id)
   716→    agents[agentIndex].deletedAt = new Date().toISOString()
   717→    agents[agentIndex].status = 'deleted'
   718→    saveAgents(agents)
   719→    invalidateAgentCache()
   720→    console.log(`[Agent Registry] Soft-deleted agent ${agentName} (id: ${id})`)
   721→    return true
   722→  }
   723→
   724→  // --- Hard-delete path: backup first, then permanently remove all data ---
   725→
   726→  // Create automatic backup before any destructive operation
   727→  backupAgentData(agentToDelete)
   728→
   729→  // Remove agent from registry
   730→  const filtered = agents.filter(a => a.id !== id)
   731→  saveAgents(filtered)
   732→  invalidateAgentCache()
   733→
   734→  // Clean up agent-specific directory (database, etc.)
   735→  const agentDir = path.join(AGENTS_DIR, id)
   736→  if (fs.existsSync(agentDir)) {
   737→    try {
   738→      fs.rmSync(agentDir, { recursive: true })
   739→    } catch (error) {
   740→      console.error(`[Agent Registry] Failed to clean up agent directory ${id}:`, error)
   741→    }
   742→  }
   743→
   744→  // Clean up message directories for this agent (legacy location)
   745→  const messageBaseDir = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'messages')
   746→  const messageBoxes = ['inbox', 'sent', 'archived']
   747→
   748→  for (const box of messageBoxes) {
   749→    co

... [436 more chars truncated]

   213→export function getAgent(id: string, includeDeleted: boolean = false): Agent | null {
   214→  const agents = loadAgents()
   215→  const agent = agents.find(a => a.id === id) || null
   216→  // If the agent is soft-deleted and caller didn't ask for deleted agents, return null
   217→  if (agent && agent.deletedAt && !includeDeleted) return null
   218→  return agent
   219→}

   191→/** Convert an AMP envelope-format message to internal Message format */
   192→function convertAMPToMessage(ampMsg: any): Message | null {
   193→  const envelope = ampMsg.envelope
   194→  const payload = ampMsg.payload
   195→  if (!envelope || !payload) return null

   214→  const status = ampMsg.metadata?.status || ampMsg.local?.status || 'unread'
   215→

   218→    from: fromName,
   219→    fromAlias: fromName,

   420→// In-memory cache for resolved agent addresses (avoids expensive 8-step resolution on every call).
   421→// Entries expire after AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS. Primary use case: when a message arrives from an external
   422→// agent, the sender's address is cached so that replies route back without re-resolving.
   423→const AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000 // 5 minutes
   424→const agentAddressCache = new Map<string, { resolved: ResolvedAgent; resolvedAt: number }>()
   425→
   426→// Proactive cache sweep every 5 minutes to prevent unbounded memory growth
   427→setInterval(() => {
   428→  const now = Date.now()
   429→  for (const [key, entry] of agentAddressCache) {
   430→    if (now - entry.resolvedAt > AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS) {
   431→      agentAddressCache.delete(key)
   432→    }
   433→  }
   434→}, 5 * 60 * 1000).unref()
   435→
   436→/**
   437→ * Resolve an agent identifier (alias, ID, session name, or name@host) to full agent info
   438→ * Supports formats:
   439→ *   - "name@host" → resolve name on specific host
   440→ *   - "uuid" → exact ID match (globally unique)
   441→ *   - "name" → resolve on self host, then any host
   442→ *   - "session_name" → parse and resolve
   443→ *
   444→ * Results are cached in-memory for 5 minutes to speed up reply routing.
   445→ *
   446→ * Priority: 1) cache hit, 2) name@host, 3) exact ID match, 4) name on self host, 5) session name, 6) partial match
   447→ */
   448→function resolveAgent(identifier: string): ResolvedAgent | null {
   449→  // Normalize cache key to lowercase since all getAgentBy* functions use case-insensitive matching;
   450→  // without this, "Alice" and "alice" would resolve to the same agent but cache as separate entries
   451→  const cacheKey = identifier.toLowerCase()
   452→
   453→  // Check in-memory cache first (avoids the expensive 8-step resolution chain)
   454→  const cached = agentAddressCache.get(cacheKey)

</details>

   652→export async function getMessage(
   653→  agentIdentifier: string,
   654→  messageId: string,
   655→  box: 'inbox' | 'sent' = 'inbox'
   656→): Promise<Message | null> {
   657→  const agent = resolveAgent(agentIdentifier)
   658→  if (!agent?.agentId) return null
   659→
   660→  // UUID-only directory lookup
   661→  const ampDir = box === 'sent' ? getAMPSentDir(agent.agentId) : getAMPInboxDir(agent.agentId)
   662→  const found = await findMessageInAMPDir(ampDir, messageId)
   663→  if (found) {
   664→    try {
   665→      const content = await fs.readFile(found.path, 'utf-8')
   666→      const ampMsg = JSON.parse(content)
   667→      if (found.isAMP) {
   668→        return convertAMPToMessage(ampMsg)
   669→      }
   670→      return ampMsg as Message
   671→    } catch {
   672→      // File read error
   673→    }
   674→  }
   675→
   676→  return null
   677→}

    57→/**
    58→ * Send a notification to a tmux session
    59→ * Uses echo to display the message without interrupting the agent's work
    60→ */
    61→async function sendTmuxNotification(sessionName: string, message: string): Promise<void> {
    62→  // Escape single quotes in the message
    63→  const escapedMessage = message.replace(/'/g, "'\\''")
    64→
    65→  // Target the first pane of the first window
    66→  const target = `${sessionName}:0.0`
    67→
    68→  // Send text and Enter atomically via tmux \; command chaining to prevent race conditions
    69→  // Uses -l (literal) flag to prevent tmux from misinterpreting key names in notification text
    70→  // Note: If the session is running a non-shell program (vim, REPL, TUI), this echo command
    71→  // will be typed as input to that program. Notifications are designed for idle shell prompts.
    72→  await execAsync(`tmux send-keys -t "${target}" -l "echo '${escapedMessage}'" \\; send-keys -t "${target}" Enter`)
    73→}
    74→

    79→  const { fromName, fromHost, subject, priority } = options
    80→
    81→  // Build sender info with optional host

    83→    ? `${fromName}@${fromHost}`
    84→    : fromName

   343→
   344→// ============================================================================
   345→// STREAMING LINE COUNTER (avoids loading entire file into memory)
   346→// ============================================================================
   347→function countFileLines(filePath: string): number {
   348→  const buffer = Buffer.alloc(64 * 1024) // 64KB read buffer
   349→  const fd = fs.openSync(filePath, 'r')
   350→  let count = 0
   351→  let bytesRead: number
   352→  let leftover = ''
   353→
   354→  try {
   355→    while ((bytesRead = fs.readSync(fd, buffer, 0, buffer.length, null)) > 0) {
   356→      const chunk = leftover + buffer.toString('utf-8', 0, bytesRead)
   357→      const lines = chunk.split('\n')
   358→      leftover = lines.pop() || ''
   359→      for (const line of lines) {
   360→        if (line.trim()) count++
   361→      }
   362→    }
   363→    if (leftover.trim()) count++
   364→  } finally {
   365→    fs.closeSync(fd)
   366→  }
   367→  return count
   368→}
   369→
   370→// ============================================================================
   371→// MAIN ENTRY: runIndexDelta — callable directly (no HTTP)
   372→// ============================================================================

   374→  success: boolean

   376→  message?: string
   377→  dry_run?: boolean
   378→  new_conversations_discovered: number
   379→  conversations_indexed?: number

  1178→export function removeSessionFromAgent(agentId: string, sessionIndex: number): boolean {
  1179→  const agents = loadAgents()
  1180→  const index = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === agentId)
  1181→
  1182→  if (index === -1) {
  1183→    return false
  1184→  }
  1185→
  1186→  if (!agents[index].sessions) {
  1187→    return false
  1188→  }
  1189→
  1190→  const sessionIdx = agents[index].sessions.findIndex(s => s.index === sessionIndex)
  1191→  if (sessionIdx === -1) {
  1192→    return false
  1193→  }
  1194→
  1195→  // Kill the tmux session first
  1196→  const agentName = agents[index].name || agents[index].alias
  1197→  if (agentName) {
  1198→    const sessionName = computeSessionName(agentName, sessionIndex)
  1199→    try {
  1200→      const { execSync } = require('child_process')
  1201→      execSync(`tmux kill-session -t "${sessionName}" 2>/dev/null || true`, { encoding: 'utf-8' })
  1202→      console.log(`[Agent Registry] Killed tmux session: ${sessionName}`)
  1203→    } catch (error) {
  1204→      // Session might not exist
  1205→    }
  1206→  }
  1207→
  1208→  // Remove from array
  1209→  agents[index].sessions.splice(sessionIdx, 1)
  1210→  agents[index].lastActive = new Date().toISOString()
  1211→
  1212→  return saveAgents(agents)
  1213→}
  1214→
  1215→// ============================================================================
  1216→// Email Identity Management
  1217→// =================================================================

  1405→/**
  1406→ * Remove an email address from an agent

  1408→export function removeEmailAddress(agentId: string, email: string): Agent {
  1409→  const agents = loadAgents()
  1410→  const index = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === agentId)
  1411→
  1412→  if (index === -1) {
  1413→    throw new Error(`Agent not found: ${agentId}`)
  1414→  }
  1415→
  1416→  const normalizedEmail = normalizeEmail(email)
  1417→
  1418→  if (!agents[index].tools?.email?.addresses) {
  1419→    throw new Error(`Agent has no email addresses`)
  1420→  }
  1421→
  1422→  const addrIndex = agents[index].tools.email.addresses.findIndex(
  1423→    a => normalizeEmail(a.address) === normalizedEmail
  1424→  )
  1425→
  1426→  if (addrIndex === -1) {
  1427→    throw new Error(`Email address not found: ${email}`)
  1428→  }
  1429→
  1430→  const wasRemovePrimary = agents[index].tools.email.addresses[addrIndex].primary
  1431→
  1432→  // Remove the address
  1433→  agents[index].tools.email.addresses.splice(addrIndex, 1)
  1434→
  1435→  // If we removed the primary, make the first remaining address primary
  1436→  if (wasRemovePrimary && agents[index].tools.email.addresses.length > 0) {
  1437→    agents[index].tools.email.addresses[0].primary = true
  1438→  }
  1439→
  1440→  agents[index].lastActive = new Date().toISOString()
  1441→  saveAgents(agents)
  1442→
  1443→  return agents[index]
  1444→}

    23→export interface Message {
    24→  id: string
    25→  from: string           // Agent ID (or session name for backward compat)
    26→  fromAlias?: string     // Agent name for addressing (e.g., "23blocks-api-auth")
    27→  fromLabel?: string     // Agent display label (e.g., "API Authentication")
    28→  fromSession?: string   // Actual session name (for delivery)
    29→  fromHost?: string      // Host ID where sender resides (e.g., 'macbook-pro', 'mac-mini')
    30→  fromVerified?: boolean // True if sender is a registered agent, false for external agents
    31→  to: string             // Agent ID (or session name for backward compat)
    32→  toAlias?: string       // Agent name for addressing
    33→  toLabel?: string       // Agent display label
    34→  toSession?: string     // Actual session name (for delivery)
    35→  toHost?: string        // Host ID where recipient resides
    36→  timestamp: string
    37→  subject: string
    38→  priority: 'low' | 'normal' | 'high' | 'urgent'
    39→  status: 'unread' | 'read' | 'archived'
    40→  content: {
    41→    type: 'request' | 'response' | 'notification' | 'update'
    42→    message: string
    43→    context?: Record<string, any>
    44→    attachments?: Array<{
    45→      name: string
    46→      path: string
    47→      type: string
    48→    }>
    49→  }
    50→  inReplyTo?: string
    51→  forwardedFrom?: {
    52→    originalMessageId: string
    53→    originalFrom: string
    54→    originalTo: string

    56→    forwardedBy: string

    64→    signatureVerified?: boolean  // True if signature was cryptographically verified

    68→}
    69→
    70→export interface MessageSummary {
    71→  id: string
    72→  from: string
    73→  fromAlias?: string

    75→  fromHost?: string
    76→  fromVerified?: boolean  // True if sender is registered, false for external agents

The summary builder at L300 reads `msg.fromLabel` which is always `undefined`. The old flat format path (L321) reads `ampMsg.fromLabel` directly from the file, which works. This means AMP-format messages will never display agent labels in the UI, while legacy flat-format messages will.

    const lookup = getAgentByName('name-reuse-test')
    expect(lookup).not.toBeNull()
    expect(lookup!.id).toBe(reused.id)
    expect(lookup!.id).not.toBe(originalId)

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:45:08]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `pr205-body.txt`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/docs_dev/pr205-body.txt"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→## Summary
     2→
     3→- **Removes** the resume flag stripping logic from `POST /api/agents/[id]/wake` that silently dropped `--continue`, `--resume`, and similar flags on first agent launch
     4→- **Bug fixed**: creating a new agent pointing at a directory with existing Claude Code conversations caused `--continue` to be stripped because `launchCount === 0` (per-agent counter, not per-project-folder) — agent started fresh instead of resuming
     5→- **Version bump**: 0.22.2 → 0.22.3
     6→
     7→## Root Cause
     8→
     9→The `isFirstLaunch` check used `agent.launchCount === 0` as a proxy for "no prior session to resume." This is fundamentally broken because `launchCount` is per-agent, not per-project-folder. A newly created agent can point at a directory that already has Claude Code conversations from manual CLI usage or other agents.
    10→
    11→## Why removal is the right fix
    12→
    13→All supported programs handle resume flags gracefully when no prior session exists:
    14→
    15→| Program | Flag | Behavior when no session exists |
    16→|---------|------|---------------------------------|
    17→| Claude Code | `--continue` | Starts a new session |
    18→| Codex | `resume --last` | Shows "no sessions" message |
    19→| Gemini | `--resume` | Starts fresh |
    20→| Aider | `--restore-chat-history` | No-op (no history file) |
    21→| OpenCode | `--continue` | Starts fresh |
    22→| Cursor | `--resume` | Starts fresh |
    23→
    24→The stripping added complexity and bugs without solving a real problem.
    25→
    26→## What changed
    27→
    28→**Removed** from `app/api/agents/[id]/wake/route.ts`:
    29→- `RESUME_PATTERNS` regex map (6 programs × multiple patterns)
    30→- `stripResumeFlags()` function
    31→- `isFirstLaunch` conditional stripping block
    32→
    33→**Kept**:
    34→- `sanitizeArgs()` shell injection protection
    35→- `launchCount` field and increment (useful metadata, just no longer drives flag decisio

... [797 more chars truncated]

</details>

   359→**First-Launch Behavior:**
   360→When an agent is woken for the first time (`launchCount` is 0), resume/continue flags are automatically stripped from `programArgs` since there is no prior session to resume. This applies per-program:
   361→- **Claude Code**: `--continue`, `-c`, `--resume`, `-r` are stripped
   362→- **Codex**: `resume --last`, `resume` are stripped
   363→- **Gemini CLI**: `--resume` is stripped
   364→- **Aider**: `--restore-chat-history` is stripped
   365→- **OpenCode**: `--continue`, `-c`, `--session`, `-s` are stripped
   366→- **Cursor**: `--resume`, `resume` are stripped
   367→
   368→On subsequent wakes (`launchCount` >= 1), full `programArgs` are used.
   369→
   370→---
   371→
   372→### 8a. Restart Agent
   373→
   374→**Command:**

</details>

<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `cozo-utils.ts`</summary>

**Result:**

     1→/**
     2→ * Shared CozoDB utilities
     3→ *
     4→ * IMPORTANT: Use these functions for ALL string values inserted into CozoDB queries.
     5→ * Raw string interpolation will break on quotes, newlines, tabs, and backslashes.
     6→ */
     7→
     8→/**
     9→ * Escape a string for safe insertion into CozoDB queries.
    10→ * Handles: backslashes, single quotes, newlines, carriage returns, tabs
    11→ *
    12→ * @param s - The string to escape (can be undefined/null)
    13→ * @returns Escaped string wrapped in quotes, or 'null' if input is falsy
    14→ *
    15→ * @example
    16→ * escapeForCozo("it's a test")  // "'it\\'s a test'"
    17→ * escapeForCozo("line1\nline2") // "'line1\\nline2'"
    18→ * escapeForCozo(undefined)      // "null"
    19→ */
    20→export function escapeForCozo(s: string | undefined | null): string {
    21→  if (!s) return 'null'
    22→
    23→  return "'" + s
    24→    .replace(/\\/g, '\\\\')   // Escape backslashes first (order matters!)
    25→    .replace(/'/g, "\\'")     // Then escape single quotes
    26→    .replace(/\n/g, '\\n')    // Then escape newlines
    27→    .replace(/\r/g, '\\r')    // Then escape carriage returns
    28→    .replace(/\t/g, '\\t')    // Then escape tabs
    29→    + "'"
    30→}
    31→
    32→/**
    33→ * Escape a string but return without quotes (for building complex expressions)
    34→ *
    35→ * @param s - The string to escape
    36→ * @returns Escaped string WITHOUT surrounding quotes
    37→ */
    38→export function escapeForCozoRaw(s: string): string {
    39→  return s
    40→    .replace(/\\/g, '\\\\')
    41→    .replace(/'/g, "\\'")
    42→    .replace(/\n/g, '\\n')
    43→    .replace(/\r/g, '\\r')
    44→    .replace(/\t/g, '\\t')
    45→}
    46→

</details>

- Inner try/catch blocks (lines 481/498 and 503/520) isolate msg_terms cleanup from code_symbols cleanup
- Orphan detection uses `not *messages{msg_id}` negation pattern (lines 485, 507) which is correct CozoDB syntax

- Comment at line 476-478 documents the crash-safety rationale

### 2. lib/rag/embeddings.ts -- APPROVED

**Singleton .catch() reset:** VERIFIED. Lines 49-54 correctly implement the retry-on-failure pattern:
```typescript
})().catch((err) => {
    extractorPromise = null;  // Reset so next call retries
    throw err;
});
```
This is correct because:
- If `pipeline()` throws, `extractor` was never assigned (line 47 only runs on success)
- Only `extractorPromise` needs resetting to allow retry
- The error is re-thrown so callers see the failure
- Without this fix, a failed initialization would permanently cache the rejected promise, and all subsequent calls would immediately fail with the same cached error

   213→export function getAgent(id: string, includeDeleted: boolean = false): Agent | null {
   214→  const agents = loadAgents()
   215→  const agent = agents.find(a => a.id === id) || null
   216→  // If the agent is soft-deleted and caller didn't ask for deleted agents, return null
   217→  if (agent && agent.deletedAt && !includeDeleted) return null
   218→  return agent
   219→}
   220→
   221→/**
   222→ * Get agent by name (the primary identity)
   223→ * Names are unique per-host, like email addresses (auth@macbook-pro ≠ auth@mac-mini)
   224→ *
   225→ * @param name - Agent name (case-insensitive)
   226→ * @param hostId - Optional host ID. If provided, searches on that host. If not, searches on self host.
   227→ */
   228→export function getAgentByName(name: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null {
   229→  const agents = loadAgents()
   230→  const normalizedName = name.toLowerCase()
   231→
   232→  if (hostId) {
   233→    // Scoped to specific host; exclude soft-deleted agents
   234→    return agents.find(a =>
   235→      !a.deletedAt &&
   236→      a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   237→      a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === hostId.toLowerCase()
   238→    ) || null
   239→  }
   240→
   241→  // Default: search on self host only; exclude soft-deleted agents
   242→  const selfHostId = getSelfHostId().toLowerCase()
   243→  return agents.find(a =>
   244→    !a.deletedAt &&
   245→    a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   246→    a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === selfHostId
   247→  ) || null
   248→}
   249→
   250→/**
   251→ * Get agent by name from ANY host (global search)
   252→ * Use sparingly - prefer getAgentByName(name, hostId) for per-host lookups
   253→ */
   254→export function getAgentByNameAnyHost(name: string): Agent | null {
   255→  const agents = loadAgents()
   256→  // Exclude soft-deleted agents from name lookups
   257→  return agents.find(a => !a.deletedAt && a.name?.toLowerCase() === name.toLowerCase()) || null

   700→export function deleteAgent(id: string, hard: boolean = false): boolean {
   701→  const agents = loadAgents()
   702→  const agentToDelete = agents.find(a => a.id === id)
   703→
   704→  if (!agentToDelete) {
   705→    return false // Agent not found
   706→  }
   707→
   708→  const agentName = agentToDelete.name || agentToDelete.alias
   709→
   710→  // Kill all tmux sessions belonging to this agent (both soft and hard delete)
   711→  killAgentSessions(agentToDelete)
   712→
   713→  if (!hard) {
   714→    // --- Soft-delete path: mark as deleted, preserve all data on disk ---
   715→    const agentIndex = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === id)
   716→    agents[agentIndex].deletedAt = new Date().toISOString()
   717→    agents[agentIndex].status = 'deleted'
   718→    saveAgents(agents)
   719→    invalidateAgentCache()
   720→    console.log(`[Agent Registry] Soft-deleted agent ${agentName} (id: ${id})`)
   721→    return true
   722→  }

   724→  // --- Hard-delete path: backup first, then permanently remove all data ---

   726→  // Create automatic backup before any destructive operation

   728→
   729→  // Remove agent from registry
   730→  const filtered = agents.filter(a => a.id !== id)
   731→  saveAgents(filtered)
   732→  invalidateAgentCache()
   733→
   734→  // Clean up agent-specific directory (database, etc.)
   735→  const agentDir = path.join(AGENTS_DIR, id)

   737→    try {
   738→      fs.rmSync(agentDir, { recursive: true })
   739→    } catch (error) {
   740→      console.error(`[Agent Registry] Failed to clean up agent directory ${id}:`, error)

   977→function normalizeTags(tags?: string[]): string[] {

   979→  return tags.map(tag => tag.toLowerCase())

   982→/**
   983→ * Search agents by query (name, label, taskDescription, tags)
   984→ */
   985→export function searchAgents(query: string): Agent[] {
   986→  const agents = loadAgents()
   987→  const lowerQuery = query.toLowerCase()
   988→
   989→  return agents.filter(a => {

   997→      a.tags?.some(tag => tag.toLowerCase().includes(lowerQuery))
   998→    )
   999→  })

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:36:05]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `pr205-body.txt`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/docs_dev/pr205-body.txt"
}
```

**Result:**

     1→## Summary
     2→
     3→- **Removes** the resume flag stripping logic from `POST /api/agents/[id]/wake` that silently dropped `--continue`, `--resume`, and similar flags on first agent launch
     4→- **Bug fixed**: creating a new agent pointing at a directory with existing Claude Code conversations caused `--continue` to be stripped because `launchCount === 0` (per-agent counter, not per-project-folder) — agent started fresh instead of resuming
     5→- **Version bump**: 0.22.2 → 0.22.3
     6→
     7→## Root Cause
     8→
     9→The `isFirstLaunch` check used `agent.launchCount === 0` as a proxy for "no prior session to resume." This is fundamentally broken because `launchCount` is per-agent, not per-project-folder. A newly created agent can point at a directory that already has Claude Code conversations from manual CLI usage or other agents.
    10→
    11→## Why removal is the right fix
    12→
    13→All supported programs handle resume flags gracefully when no prior session exists:
    14→
    15→| Program | Flag | Behavior when no session exists |
    16→|---------|------|---------------------------------|
    17→| Claude Code | `--continue` | Starts a new session |
    18→| Codex | `resume --last` | Shows "no sessions" message |
    19→| Gemini | `--resume` | Starts fresh |

   358→
   359→**First-Launch Behavior:**
   360→When an agent is woken for the first time (`launchCount` is 0), resume/continue flags are automatically stripped from `programArgs` since there is no prior session to resume. This applies per-program:
   361→- **Claude Code**: `--continue`, `-c`, `--resume`, `-r` are stripped
   362→- **Codex**: `resume --last`, `resume` are stripped
   363→- **Gemini CLI**: `--resume` is stripped
   364→- **Aider**: `--restore-chat-history` is stripped
   365→- **OpenCode**: `--continue`, `-c`, `--session`, `-s` are stripped
   366→- **Cursor**: `--resume`, `resume` are stripped
   367→
   368→On subsequent wakes (`launchCount` >= 1), full `programArgs` are used.
   369→
   370→---

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:38:32]*

I've now verified everything. Let me trace the additional bug in the regex: The `-c` pattern `/\s*-c\b(?!\s*\S)/g` uses a negative lookahead `(?!\s*\S)` which means "not followed by optional whitespace then a non-whitespace character" -- effectively meaning `-c` is only matched when it's at the end of the string or followed by only whitespace. But `--continue` would already be caught by the first regex, so `-c` is the short form. The regex is actually overly conservative (it tries not to match `-c` when followed by another argument), but the fundamental issue is the `isFirstLaunch` logic being broken as the PR describes.

Now let me write the audit report.

I'll write the output file directly. Since I'm a judge agent with no Bash tool, I'll structure the output for the orchestrator. Let me check if there's a way to write...

Let me re-read the tools available -- I have Read, Grep, and Glob. I don't have a write/edit tool. I'll provide the full audit inline since I cannot write to a file.

# Refactoring Review: PR #205 - Remove Broken Resume Flag Stripping
Generated: 2026-02-15
Reviewer: judge-agent

## Verdict: APPROVED (with one advisory note)

## Summary
**PR Goal:** Remove broken resume flag stripping logic from the wake route
**Goal Achieved:** Yes
**Behavior Preserved:** Yes -- the removed behavior was actively harmful (stripping user-intended flags)

## Audit Checklist

### 1. Diff reads correctly against current file state -- VERIFIED

The code to be removed exists exactly as shown in the diff at `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/app/api/agents/[id]/wake/route.ts` lines 198-239. The `RESUME_PATTERNS` dict (line 199), `stripResumeFlags` function (line 208), and `isFirstLaunch` conditional block (line 229) are all present and match the diff character-for-character.

### 2. Removed code was genuinely broken -- VERIFIED

The bug is real and confirmed by tracing the logic:
- New agents are created with `launchCount: 0` (verified in `lib/agent-registry.ts:413`)
- The `isFirstLaunch` check (`!agent.launchCount || agent.launchCount === 0`) triggers on every newly created agent
- This means: creating a new agent pointing at a directory WITH existing Claude Code conversations would strip `--continue`, preventing the user from resuming those conversations
- `launchCount` is per-agent, not per-project-folder -- it cannot reliably indicate whether a prior session exists
- The PR description's claim that all supported programs handle resume flags gracefully when no session exists is correct (Claude Code's `--continue` starts fresh if no prior session)

### 3. No dangling references to removed functions/types -- VERIFIED

- `stripResumeFlags` and `RESUME_PATTERNS` are locally scoped inside the POST handler -- no external callers exist (confirmed via grep across entire codebase)
- `sanitizeArgs` is preserved (not removed)
- `launchCount` field and its increment at line 278 are preserved
- `launchCount` type definition in `types/agent.ts:181` remains

    28→

    30→    fs.appendFileSync(crashLogPath, logEntry)
    31→  } catch (fsError) {
    32→    // Ignore file write errors
    33→  }
    34→
    35→  // Don't exit - allow the server to continue running
    36→  // Only exit for truly fatal errors
    37→  if (error.code === 'EADDRINUSE' || error.code === 'EACCES') {

    39→    process.exit(1)
    40→  }
    41→})

     1→#!/bin/bash
     2→# AI Maestro Common Shell Helper Functions
     3→# Shared utilities for all agent scripts
     4→#
     5→# Usage: source "$(dirname "$0")/../scripts/shell-helpers/common.sh"
     6→# Or for installed scripts: source ~/.local/share/aimaestro/shell-helpers/common.sh
     7→
     8→HOSTS_CONFIG="${HOME}/.aimaestro/hosts.json"
     9→
    10→# Hosts config is cached in a simple format (no associative arrays for compatibility)
    11→_HOSTS_LOADED=""
    12→_SELF_HOST_ID=""
    13→_SELF_HOST_URL=""
    14→
    15→# Get this machine's host ID and URL from the identity API or hosts.json
    16→# Sets: _SELF_HOST_ID, _SELF_HOST_URL
    17→_init_self_host() {
    18→    # Already initialized
    19→    if [ -n "$_SELF_HOST_ID" ]; then
    20→        return 0
    21→    fi
    22→
    23→    # Try identity API first (most reliable)
    24→    local identity
    25→    identity=$(curl -s --max-time 5 "http://127.0.0.1:23000/api/hosts/identity" 2>/dev/null)
    26→    if [ -n "$identity" ]; then
    27→        _SELF_HOST_ID=$(echo "$identity" | jq -r '.host.id // empty' 2>/dev/null)
    28→        _SELF_HOST_URL=$(echo "$identity" | jq -r '.host.url // empty' 2>/dev/null)
    29→        if [ -n "$_SELF_HOST_ID" ] && [ -n "$_SELF_HOST_URL" ]; then
    30→            return 0
    31→        fi
    32→    fi
    33→
    34→    # Fallback: Find local host in hosts.json
    35→    if [ -f "$HOSTS_CONFIG" ]; then
    36→        local local_host
    37→        local_host=$(jq -r '.hosts[] | select(.type == "local") | "\(.id)|\(.url)"' "$HOSTS_CONFIG" 2>/dev/null | head -1)
    38→        if [ -n "$local_host" ]; then
    39→            _SELF_HOST_ID="${local_host%%|*}"
    40→            _SELF_HOST_URL="${local_host#*|}"
    41→            return 0
    42→        fi
    43→    fi
    44→
    45→    # Last resort: Use hostname
    46→    _SELF_HOST_ID=$(hostname | tr '[:upper:]' '[:lower:]')
    47→    _SELF_HOST_URL="http://${_SELF_HOST_ID}:23000"
    48→}

**Detailed Analysis:**

**1. server.mjs -- tmux quoting**

- Line 700: `pty.spawn('tmux', ['attach-session', '-t', sessionName], ...)` -- This uses array arguments to `pty.spawn`, so each argument is a separate element. `sessionName` is passed as its own array element, meaning it is NOT subject to shell word-splitting. This is **correct** and does NOT need double quotes (it is not a shell command, it is a direct exec).
- Line 840: `` `tmux capture-pane -t "${sessionName}" -p -S -2000 2>/dev/null || tmux capture-pane -t "${sessionName}" -p` `` -- This is a **shell command** string passed to `exec()`. The `${sessionName}` is inside **double-quoted** template literal AND wrapped in `"${sessionName}"` -- **correctly quoted**.

VERDICT: server.mjs is CLEAN. All tmux `-t` targets are properly handled.

**2. agent-container/agent-server.js -- tmux target quoting**

There are 4 tmux `-t` references in shell commands:
- Line 107: `tmux has-session -t "${SESSION_NAME}" 2>&1` -- **quoted, OK**
- Line 114: `tmux new-session -d -s ${SESSION_NAME} -c ${WORKSPACE}` -- **BUG: UNQUOTED** `-s ${SESSION_NAME}` and `-c ${WORKSPACE}`. If `SESSION_NAME` or `WORKSPACE` contain spaces, this will break.
- Line 119: `tmux send-keys -t "${SESSION_NAME}" "${AI_TOOL}" C-m` -- **quoted, OK**
- Line 147: `tmux capture-pane -t "${sessionKey}"` -- **quoted, OK**
- Line 162: `pty.spawn('tmux', ['attach-session', '-t', sessionKey], ...)` -- Array arguments, no quoting needed, **OK**.
- Line 177: `tmux capture-pane -t "${sessionKey}"` -- **quoted, OK**

**ISSUE FOUND**: Line 114 has unquoted `${SESSION_NAME}` and `${WORKSPACE}`.

    18→function debounce<T extends (...args: unknown[]) => void>(fn: T, ms: number): T {
    19→  let timeoutId: ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> | null = null
    20→  return ((...args: unknown[]) => {
    21→    if (timeoutId) clearTimeout(timeoutId)
    22→    timeoutId = setTimeout(() => fn(...args), ms)
    23→  }) as T
    24→}

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:46:10]*

This is significant. The `terminal.onSelectionChange()` at line 275 returns a disposable, but it is NOT captured or disposed. However, since `terminal.dispose()` is called in the cleanup function (line 295), and xterm.js's `dispose()` method clears all registered event listeners internally, this is safe -- xterm.js handles this automatically when the terminal is disposed.

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:46:23]*

The debounce function at line 18-24 creates a closure over `timeoutId`. When `ResizeObserver` is disconnected (line 286 in cleanup), no more calls to `debouncedFit` will occur. However, if a debounce timer was already scheduled when cleanup runs, it will still fire after cleanup. The timer references `fitAddonRef.current` and `terminalRef.current`, both of which are set to `null` in cleanup (lines 297-298). The `debouncedFit` callback checks for both refs before calling `.fit()` (line 184), so a late-firing timer is harmless -- it checks the nulled refs and does nothing.

Now let me verify the `setTimeout` in the `handleDelete` of `DeleteAgentDialog.tsx` for the unmount race condition.

The `handleDelete` function at line 32-53 has a `setTimeout` at line 42 that calls `onClose()` and state setters after 1500ms. If the component unmounts before the timeout fires, calling `setPhase`, `setConfirmText`, and `setDeleting` on an unmounted component would be a no-op in React 18+ (no warning, no error), but `onClose()` could still execute a parent state update on an unmounted tree. This is a minor concern -- in practice the dialog stays mounted for the 1500ms because it is showing the "done" animation phase. But strictly speaking, there is no cleanup for this timeout.

Let me also check one more thing -- the `setSendData(null)` cleanup in TerminalView.tsx:

**Findings across all 4 files:**

**1. app/page.tsx** -- `resizeTimeoutRef` pattern is correct: declared as `useRef` (line 89), cleaned up on unmount (line 202), cleared before re-set in `toggleSidebar` (line 499). `setSidebarCollapsed` uses functional setState `prev => !prev` (line 495). No memory leaks.

**2. components/DeleteAgentDialog.tsx** -- Export prompt with download present (lines 173-194). Export button disabled during both `exporting` and `deleting` states (line 184: `disabled={exporting || deleting}`). Delete button cross-disables during `exporting` (line 221: `disabled={confirmText !== agentAlias || deleting || exporting}`). Empty blob check at line 76-78 (`blob.size === 0`). One minor issue: `setTimeout` at line 42 (1500ms auto-close after delete) has no cleanup -- if component unmounts early, state setters fire on unmounted component. React 18 silently ignores this, so no crash, but it is technically unclean.

**3. components/TerminalView.tsx** -- `setSendData` sync effect (lines 198-205) correctly syncs with WebSocket connection state: sets `sendMessage` when connected, `null` when disconnected, and cleans up with `return () => setSendData(null)`. Dependencies `[isConnected, sendMessage, setSendData]` are complete. No stale closure risk.

**4. hooks/useTerminal.ts** -- Cmd+C copy/SIGINT fallthrough at lines 237-248: checks `terminal.getSelection()`, copies if selection exists and returns `false` (blocks SIGINT), falls through to `return true` (line 270) when no selection (allows SIGINT). Correct. Cmd+V paste via bracketed paste at lines 252-268: reads clipboard, normalizes line endings, wraps in `\x1b[200~`/`\x1b[201~`, sends via `sendDataRef.current`. Returns `false` to prevent browser paste. Correct. Auto-copy selection at lines 275-282: triggers on selection >= 3 chars. The `onSelectionChange` disposable is not captured, but this is safe because `terminal.dispose()` (line 295) cleans up all xterm.js event listeners internally. Debounce timer in `debouncedFit` (line 183) could fire after cleanup, but the callback guards against null refs (line 184). No memory leaks.

**One actionable issue found**: DeleteAgentDialog.tsx line 42 `setTimeout` lacks cleanup. Should store in a ref and clear on unmount/close.

   213→export function getAgent(id: string, includeDeleted: boolean = false): Agent | null {
   214→  const agents = loadAgents()
   215→  const agent = agents.find(a => a.id === id) || null
   216→  // If the agent is soft-deleted and caller didn't ask for deleted agents, return null
   217→  if (agent && agent.deletedAt && !includeDeleted) return null
   218→  return agent
   219→}
   220→
   221→/**
   222→ * Get agent by name (the primary identity)
   223→ * Names are unique per-host, like email addresses (auth@macbook-pro ≠ auth@mac-mini)
   224→ *
   225→ * @param name - Agent name (case-insensitive)
   226→ * @param hostId - Optional host ID. If provided, searches on that host. If not, searches on self host.
   227→ */
   228→export function getAgentByName(name: string, hostId?: string): Agent | null {
   229→  const agents = loadAgents()
   230→  const normalizedName = name.toLowerCase()
   231→
   232→  if (hostId) {
   233→    // Scoped to specific host; exclude soft-deleted agents
   234→    return agents.find(a =>
   235→      !a.deletedAt &&
   236→      a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   237→      a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === hostId.toLowerCase()
   238→    ) || null
   239→  }
   240→
   241→  // Default: search on self host only; exclude soft-deleted agents
   242→  const selfHostId = getSelfHostId().toLowerCase()
   243→  return agents.find(a =>
   244→    !a.deletedAt &&
   245→    a.name?.toLowerCase() === normalizedName &&
   246→    a.hostId?.toLowerCase() === selfHostId
   247→  ) || null
   248→}
   249→
   250→/**
   251→ * Get agent by name from ANY host (global search)
   252→ * Use sparingly - prefer getAgentByName(name, hostId) for per-host lookups
   253→ */
   254→export function getAgentByNameAnyHost(name: string): Agent | null {
   255→  const agents = loadAgents()
   256→  // Exclude soft-deleted agents from name lookups
   257→  return agents.find(a => !a.deletedAt && a.name?.toLowerCase() === name.toLowerCase()) || null

   700→export function deleteAgent(id: string, hard: boolean = false): boolean {
   701→  const agents = loadAgents()
   702→  const agentToDelete = agents.find(a => a.id === id)
   703→
   704→  if (!agentToDelete) {
   705→    return false // Agent not found
   706→  }
   707→
   708→  const agentName = agentToDelete.name || agentToDelete.alias
   709→
   710→  // Kill all tmux sessions belonging to this agent (both soft and hard delete)
   711→  killAgentSessions(agentToDelete)
   712→
   713→  if (!hard) {
   714→    // --- Soft-delete path: mark as deleted, preserve all data on disk ---
   715→    const agentIndex = agents.findIndex(a => a.id === id)
   716→    agents[agentIndex].deletedAt = new Date().toISOString()
   717→    agents[agentIndex].status = 'deleted'
   718→    saveAgents(agents)
   719→    invalidateAgentCache()
   720→    console.log(`[Agent Registry] Soft-deleted agent ${agentName} (id: ${id})`)
   721→    return true
   722→  }
   723→
   724→  // --- Hard-delete path: backup first, then permanently remove all data ---
   725→
   726→  // Create automatic backup before any destructive operation
   727→  backupAgentData(agentToDelete)
   728→
   729→  // Remove agent from registry
   730→  const filtered = agents.filter(a => a.id !== id)
   731→  saveAgents(filtered)
   732→  invalidateAgentCache()
   733→
   734→  // Clean up agent-specific directory (database, etc.)
   735→  const agentDir = path.join(AGENTS_DIR, id)
   736→  if (fs.existsSync(agentDir)) {
   737→    try {
   738→      fs.rmSync(agentDir, { recursive: true })
   739→    } catch (error) {
   740→      console.error(`[Agent Registry] Failed to clean up agent directory ${id}:`, error)
   741→    }
   742→  }
   743→
   744→  // Clean up message directories for this agent (legacy location)
   745→  const messageBaseDir = path.join(AIMAESTRO_DIR, 'messages')
   746→  const messageBoxes = ['inbox', 'sent', 'archived']
   747→
   748→  for (const box of messageBoxes) {
   749→    co

   787→export function listAgents(includeDeleted: boolean = false): AgentSummary[] {
   788→  const agents = loadAgents()
   789→  const filtered = includeDeleted ? agents : agents.filter(a => !a.deletedAt)
   790→
   791→  return filtered.map(a => {
   792→    const agentName = a.name || a.alias || 'unknown'
   793→    const sessions: AgentSession[] = a.sessions || []
   794→
   795→    // Find first online session for deprecated currentSession field
   796→    const onlineSession = sessions.find(s => s.status === 'online')
   797→    const currentSession = onlineSession ? computeSessionName(agentName, onlineSession.index) : undefined
   798→
   799→    return {
   800→      id: a.id,
   801→      name: agentName,
   802→      label: a.label,
   803→      avatar: a.avatar,
   804→      hostId: a.hostId || getSelfHostId(),
   805→      hostUrl: a.hostUrl,
   806→      status: a.status,
   807→      lastActive: a.lastActive,
   808→      sessions,
   809→      deployment: a.deployment,
   810→      deletedAt: a.deletedAt,
   811→      // DEPRECATED: for backward compatibility
   812→      alias: agentName,
   813→      currentSession,
   814→    }
   815→  })
   816→}

  it('getAgent() returns null for soft-deleted agent', () => {

   105→ * Ensures no duplicate avatars on the same host
   106→ */
   107→function generateUniqueAvatarUrl(agentId: string, usedAvatars: Set<string>): string {
   108→  const hash = computeHash(agentId)
   109→  const gender = getGenderFromId(agentId) === 'male' ? 'men' : 'women'
   110→
   111→  // Start with hash-based index, find next available
   112→  let index = Math.abs(hash) % 100
   113→  let attempts = 0
   114→
   115→  while (attempts < 100) {
   116→    const url = `/avatars/${gender}_${index.toString().padStart(2, '0')}.png`
   117→    if (!usedAvatars.has(url)) {
   118→      return url
   119→    }
   120→    index = (index + 1) % 100
   121→    attempts++
   122→  }
   123→
   124→  // Fallback if all 100 are used (unlikely)
   125→  return `/avatars/${gender}_${(Math.abs(hash) % 100).toString().padStart(2, '0')}.png`
   126→}
   127→

   134→  }

   420→// In-memory cache for resolved agent addresses (avoids expensive 8-step resolution on every call).
   421→// Entries expire after AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS. Primary use case: when a message arrives from an external
   422→// agent, the sender's address is cached so that replies route back without re-resolving.
   423→const AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000 // 5 minutes
   424→const agentAddressCache = new Map<string, { resolved: ResolvedAgent; resolvedAt: number }>()
   425→
   426→// Proactive cache sweep every 5 minutes to prevent unbounded memory growth
   427→setInterval(() => {
   428→  const now = Date.now()
   429→  for (const [key, entry] of agentAddressCache) {
   430→    if (now - entry.resolvedAt > AGENT_CACHE_TTL_MS) {
   431→      agentAddressCache.delete(key)
   432→    }
   433→  }
   434→}, 5 * 60 * 1000).unref()
   435→
   436→/**
   437→ * Resolve an agent identifier (alias, ID, session name, or name@host) to full agent info
   438→ * Supports formats:
   439→ *   - "name@host" → resolve name on specific host
   440→ *   - "uuid" → exact ID match (globally unique)
   441→ *   - "name" → resolve on self host, then any host
   442→ *   - "session_name" → parse and resolve
   443→ *
   444→ * Results are cached in-memory for 5 minutes to speed up reply routing.
   445→ *
   446→ * Priority: 1) cache hit, 2) name@host, 3) exact ID match, 4) name on self host, 5) session name, 6) partial match
   447→ */
   448→function resolveAgent(identifier: string): ResolvedAgent | null {
   449→  // Normalize cache key to lowercase since all getAgentBy* functions use case-insensitive matching;
   450→  // without this, "Alice" and "alice" would resolve to the same agent but cache as separate entries
   451→  const cacheKey = identifier.toLowerCase()
   452→
   453→  // Check in-memory cache first (avoids the expensive 8-step resolution chain)
   454→  const cached = agentAddressCache.get(cacheKey)
   455→  if (cached && (Date.now() - cached.resolvedAt) < AGENT_CA

... [6219 more chars truncated]

    45→  }

    47→
    48→/**
    49→ * Check if tmux pane is in copy-mode and cancel it if so
    50→ */
    51→async function cancelCopyModeIfActive(sessionName: string): Promise<void> {
    52→  try {
    53→    // Check if we're in copy-mode by querying the pane mode
    54→    const { stdout } = await execAsync(`tmux display-message -t "${sessionName}" -p "#{pane_in_mode}"`)
    55→    const inMode = stdout.trim() === '1'
    56→
    57→    if (inMode) {
    58→      // Send 'q' to exit copy-mode
    59→      await execAsync(`tmux send-keys -t "${sessionName}" q`)
    60→      // Small delay for mode to exit
    61→      await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 50))
    62→    }
    63→  } catch {
    64→    // Ignore errors - session might not exist or other issue
    65→  }
    66→}
    67→
    68→/**
    69→ * Send keys to a tmux session using tmux send-keys
    70→ * This works regardless of whether we have a PTY connection
    71→ */
    72→async function sendKeysToTmux(sessionName: string, keys: string): Promise<void> {
    73→  // Cancel copy-mode if active (otherwise the 'q' would be typed)
    74→  await cancelCopyModeIfActive(sessionName)
    75→
    76→  // Use -l for literal text (treats keys as literal characters, not key names)
    77→  // Escape single quotes for shell safety
    78→  const escapedKeys = keys.replace(/'/g, "'\\''")
    79→  await execAsync(`tmux send-keys -t "${sessionName}" -l '${escapedKeys}'`)
    80→}
    81→

    83→ * POST /api/sessions/[id]/command
    84→ * Send a command to a terminal session via tmux send-keys

    87→ * - command: string - The command to send

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:37:38]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Read -- `agent-registry.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

```json
{
  "file_path": "/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/agent-registry.ts",
  "offset": 1005,
  "limit": 40
}
```

**Result:**

  1005→ * Used for messaging and other operations that reference agents by name
  1006→ *
  1007→ * @param nameOrId - Agent name, name@host, or UUID
  1008→ * @param defaultHostId - Optional default host if not specified in nameOrId
  1009→ */
  1010→export function resolveAlias(nameOrId: string, defaultHostId?: string): string | null {
  1011→  // Check for name@host format
  1012→  if (nameOrId.includes('@')) {
  1013→    const [name, hostId] = nameOrId.split('@')
  1014→    const agent = getAgentByName(name, hostId)
  1015→    return agent?.id || null
  1016→  }
  1017→
  1018→  // Try by UUID first (globally unique)
  1019→  const byId = getAgent(nameOrId)
  1020→  if (byId) {
  1021→    return byId.id
  1022→  }
  1023→
  1024→  // Try by name on specified or self host
  1025→  const hostId = defaultHostId || getSelfHostId()

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:38:49]*

Good -- the `sendFromUI` function propagates `fromLabel`/`toLabel`, falling back to `displayName` from the resolved agent. The issue raised in the audit question was specifically about `convertAMPToMessage` in messageQueue.ts. Let me verify: the AMP envelope format does NOT store `fromLabel`/`toLabel` fields in the envelope (they're just `from`/`to` addresses). The `convertAMPToMessage` function at line 216 returns `fromAlias: fromName` but no `fromLabel`/`toLabel`. However, when reading from `collectMessagesFromAMPDir` (line 300-304), the diff ADDED `fromLabel: msg.fromLabel` and `toLabel: msg.toLabel` propagation for the AMP envelope path. Since `convertAMPToMessage` returns a Message with undefined `fromLabel`/`toLabel`, those fields will be `undefined` in the summary -- which is correct behavior because the AMP envelope truly doesn't contain labels. The old flat format (line 321-326) reads `fromLabel: ampMsg.fromLabel` and `toLabel: ampMsg.toLabel` directly from the stored JSON, which is also correct.

Now let me write the final audit report.

   313→    // Using send-keys with -l (literal) to avoid interpreting special characters
   314→    // Text and Enter are sent atomically via tmux \; command chaining to prevent race conditions
   315→    const tmuxCommand = `tmux send-keys -t "${sessionName}" -l '${escapedMessage}' \\; send-keys -t "${sessionName}" Enter`
   316→

   318→    await execAsync(tmuxCommand)

## <span style="color:#4CAF50">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-15 20:39:20]*

This is correct. When text is wrapped in single quotes in shell, only single quotes need escaping. The `-l` flag makes tmux treat the content as literal text (no key name interpretation). The old code was over-escaping by also escaping `\`, `"`, `$`, and backticks -- which was actually wrong when inside single quotes because those characters are literal in single-quoted strings.

I'll write the report to the specified output file.
